TI Integration of Customer Experience Management into the DNA of a Service
   Enterprise
SO 2007 IEEE INTERNATIONAL ENGINEERING MANAGEMENT CONFERENCE
LA English
DT Proceedings Paper
CT IEEE International Engineering Management Conference
CY JUL 29-AUG 01, 2007
CL Lost Pines, TX
SP IEEE
DE Customer experience management; innovation management; service
   innovation management; total innovation management
ID INNOVATION
AB Integrating customer experience management (CEM) into the DNA of an enterprise allows a company to recognize innovation opportunities that will potentially make their service unique. It will also assist the company in implementing those innovative ideas by focusing on their customers' needs and wants. Moreover, integration of total innovation management (TIM) and CEM will help in reforming the service industry's culture by allowing all employees to constantly contribute to ongoing innovation efforts at any time and any place. Currently, TIM has a product innovation focus. Integrating CEM and TIM partners the customer focus with the enterprise-wide innovation ecosystem and allows for the customer's experience to become the focal point of every activity throughout a company, thus making TIM more applicable in a service enterprise. This paper surveys the existing research conducted on innovation management, total innovation management, and customer experience management. This paper summarizes innovation management and how it initiated TIM and discusses the importance of Customer Experience Management (CEM) for a service enterprise. Furthermore, it proposes that incorporating TIM and CEM must be the focal point in a service enterprise's day-to-day business activities.

TI Directed basic research
SO NATIONAL ACADEMY SCIENCE LETTERS-INDIA
LA English
DT Article; Proceedings Paper
CT 76th Annual Session of the National-Academy-of-Sciences
CY OCT   06, 2006
CL Indian Inst Technol, Bombay, INDIA
SP Natl Acad Sci
HO Indian Inst Technol
AB In its execution, and in the requirement of no other deliverables than knowledge generation, 'directed basic research' is no different from conventional (self-directed) basic research. The selected areas are determined in a national perspective. 'Directed Basic Research' may be in an area where the knowledge generation would benefit Indian Society in the long term. or it may be in an area where the results of the research would benefit Indian Industry or our strategic interests in the long term.
   India can become a global innovation leader provided we have 'technology foresight' to make the right technology choices, provided we introduce 'coherent synergy' (a phrase I coined a few years back in this context) in our science and technology related activities and provided we establish an effective innovation ecosystem'. 'We must also selectively promote some technology areas through 'directed basic research'.
   Sustainable economic development in the future requires strong and increased funding of basic research. While directed basic research should be encouraged, self-directed basic research should also receive substantially increased support.

TI The concept of entropy and the performance entropy of regional
   technological innovation ecosystem
SO PROCEEDINGS OF 2007 INTERNATIONAL CONFERENCE ON MANAGEMENT SCIENCE &

LA English
DT Proceedings Paper

DE entropy; factor analysis; performance of regional technology innovation

AB The study of the regional technology innovation ecosystem (RTIE) derives from the revelation on the natural ecological system. This paper, proceeding from the basic thinking of the entropy theory, discusses the idea of entropy of RTIE and advances the concept of performance entropy with the analysis of the structure of performance entropy flow and the structures of performance entropy. And based on the soft thinking methodology (SSM), we build up the indicator system for the evaluation of regional technology innovation performance, and then the computation of performance entropy of the technology innovation ecosystem in terms of administrative region is provided through the building of relevant models (Entropy analysis and Factor analysis). Finally we use Rank Correlation method to verify the degree of relationship between the two evaluation methods.

TI Making a case on statistical design of experiments as a tool to predict
   a firm's awareness of intellectual capital
SO PROCEEDINGS OF THE 8TH EUROPEAN CONFERENCE ON KNOWLEDGE MANAGEMENT, VOL
   1 AND 2
LA English
DT Proceedings Paper
CT 8th European Conference on Knowledge Management
CY SEP 06-07, 2007
CL Consorci Escola Ind, Barcelona, SPAIN
SP ACL
HO Consorci Escola Ind
DE intellectual capital; superior performance; perceptions; statistical
   design of experiment
AB Increasing competitive pressure, the constantly accelerating transformation of the economy, and a stronger focus on value added have initiated the search for sustainable sources of competitive advantage. In this context, innovation has emerged as the new paradigm of superior performance, and economically useful knowledge (i.e. intellectual capital, IC) has become the crucial component to be systematically managed. Many contributions in the field of the resource-and knowledge-based view have categorised intangible resources and described their influence on the company's performance. Among one such resources and capabilities the company's skills and abilities to develop the necessary networks (i.e. relational capital, RC). Equally important are the company's abilities to: a) nurture and manage the innovation and management competencies (i.e. human capital, HC), b) count on processes and systems that support and enable the firm's knowledge platform and knowledge transfer; and c) promote the type of values and norms that enable and facilitate joint interaction, knowledge sharing, idea generation, and continuous learning, and build a governance system that is consistent with this (i.e. structural capital, SC); and, last but not least, d) elaborate on a business model that while managing and developing all three IC factors, leverages the whole firm's innovation ecosystem. This is particularly key for SMEs-almost 100% of European firms, RICARDIS (2006)-whose little slack could seriously constrain their innovation potential and jeopardise their survival in the long run.
   Developing a business scenario that accounts for innovation and both its enablers and facilitators (HC, SC, RC), implies that the 'real' business scenario the individual shapes from his/her values and cognitions and in interaction with the environment also regard these elements as important. This study is an attempt to analyse the extent to which a group of potential managers perceives the market demands for innovation, and the IC elements that enable it, as important ingredients of the Spanish firms' business reality. To test this hypothesis a statistical design experiment (SIDE was conducted among 112 technical engineering students in their final career years at the EUETIB-UPC. The findings show that they have an incomplete and torn representation of the business world. This has important implications for Spanish firms' competitiveness.

PT J
AU Adner, R
AF Adner, R
TI Match your innovation strategy to your innovation ecosystem
SO HARVARD BUSINESS REVIEW
LA English
DT Article
AB High-definition televisions should, by now be a huge success. Philips, Sony, and Thompson invested billions of dollars to develop TV sets with astonishing picture quality. From a technology perspective, they've succeeded: Console manufacturers have been ready for the mass market since the early 1990s. Yet the category has been an unmitigated failure, not because of deficiencies, but because critical complements such as studio production equipment were not developed or adopted in time. Under-performing complements have left console producers in the position of offering a Ferrari in a world without gasoline or highways-an admirable engineering feat, but not one that creates value for customers.
   The HDTV story exemplifies the promise and peril of innovation ecosystems-the collaborative arrangements through which firms combine their individual offers into a coherent, customer-facing solution. When they work, innovation ecosystems allow companies to create value that no one firm could have created alone. The benefits of these systems are real. But for many organizations the attempt at ecosystem innovation has been a costly failure. This is because, along with new opportunities, innovation ecosystems also present a new set of risks that can brutally derail a firm's best efforts.
   Innovation ecosystems are characterized by three fundamental types of risk: initiative risks-the familiar uncertainties of managing a project; interdependence risks the uncertainties of coordinating with complementary innovators; and integration risks-the uncertainties presented by the adoption process across the value chain. Firms that assess ecosystem risks holistically and systematically will be able to establish more realistic expectations, develop a more refined set of environmental contingencies, and arrive at a more robust innovation strategy. Collectively, these actions will lead to more effective implementation and more profitable innovation.

SO TECHNOLOGY MANAGEMENT FOR RESHAPING THE WORLD

DE ecosystem; regional technological innovation ecosystem; adaptation;
   restrictive factors
AB This paper, combining the theories of ecology and the regional technological innovation system (RTIS), first advances a new concept: the regional technological innovation ecosystem (RTIE), which consists of the composite organizations and the organizations with a composite environment for regional technological innovation.
